Local News

Various Sectors Organize to Rescue Flood Victims

▲Propaganda... Fundraising... Relief Distribution... Epidemic Prevention

This year, floods have caused disasters in various locations, affecting as many as sixteen or seventeen provinces, with the number of victims reaching fifty to sixty million. This is truly unprecedented in over a hundred years. Relief organizations of officials and civilians in this city have been established one after another. The various news received yesterday was complex and varied, but can be summarized as propaganda, fundraising, relief distribution, and epidemic prevention. These are compiled and recorded as follows:

▲Officials and Civilians Rise Up to Cooperatively Provide Disaster Relief

▲Relief Committee Dispatches Personnel to Provide Urgent Relief

The Relief Affairs Committee is making every effort to provide relief for the floods in various provinces. Previously, Chairman Xu Shiying obtained two million yuan in salt tax treasury bonds from the central government, and has already borrowed one million yuan in cash by mortgaging them to Shanghai banking circles for urgent relief use. Personnel for relief distribution have been assigned separately, and relief fund allocation will be handled in accordance with the meeting's resolutions. All matters regarding relief distribution telegrams and relief distribution items have been submitted to the Ministry of Transportation to instruct the provinces to take note. It is reported that the dispatched committee members, Wang Zhen for Jiangsu and Zhejiang, and Xie Zhuang for Anhui and Jiangxi, according to a telegram from Nanjing, have already departed from Beijing. Li Huanying for Hunan and Wang Shouzhen for Henan will depart from Beijing by train tonight. Li Jin and Guan Huai, concerned about the severity of the disaster in Hankou, departed from Shanghai by plane this morning to provide emergency relief in Hankou. All relief distribution personnel have uniformly shipped relief supplies and relief tickets, medicines, etc., in advance, and have set off separately. Furthermore, the committee received a telegram yesterday from the Henan Relief Affairs Committee, addressed to Mr. Wang Yilao of the Relief Committee's Shanghai Office, and forwarded to Mr. Du Yuesheng, Mr. Wu Zhihao, and Mr. Yu Qiaqing: "The people of Henan, surviving soldiers and bandits, have once again fallen into a great calamity. Since the beginning of summer this year, there has been too much rainfall, and dozens of rivers, including the Huai, Sha, and Luo, have successively overflowed. Currently, it has been found that there are already fifty-four affected counties, including Xin, Yan, Luo, and Shang. The losses of the people are immeasurable, truly a unique disaster in history. This committee is responsible for providing relief and cannot sleep soundly. However, the disaster area is too large, and funds are unavailable. The central government has promised to allocate relief funds, but repeated telegrams have been sent requesting them, and they have not yet been issued. Twenty million disaster victims are daily in deep water, crying out for food. We dare not evade blame for the criticisms from all sides. In addition to dispatching personnel to various counties that have not been affected by the floods to raise funds, we are also recommending Chairman Zhang Boying of this committee to personally go to Beijing and Shanghai to plead with the government and various charitable organizations of the Relief Committee on behalf of the dying famine victims. We urge our fellow countrymen to provide strong assistance and facilitate their progress. We hope for your benevolence and will offer endless prayers. This special telegram is sent to you, hoping for your clear understanding. The Henan Relief Affairs Committee bows in respect."

▲Establishment of the Liaison Group of the Flood Relief Committee

In view of the floods in various provinces and the urgent need for relief, the National Government has specially established a Flood Relief Committee, appointing Song Ziwen, Xu Shiying, Liu Shangqing, Kong Xiangxi, and Zhu Qinglan as government committee members. Seven groups have been established, namely Investigation, Finance, Accounting, Audit, Hygiene, Epidemic Prevention, Transportation, Liaison, and Disaster Area Work. Each group has a director, appointed by the committee members. Minister of Industry Kong Xiangxi serves as the director of the Liaison Group. Regulations have been drafted, dividing the work into five sections. Xu Jianping has been appointed as the director of the General Affairs Section, Liu Kuidu as the director of the Documentation Section, Guo Bingwen as the director of the Coordination Section, Mu Xiangyue as the director of the Investigation Section, and Zou Bingwen as the director of the Propaganda Section. Furthermore, more than sixty people, including Lu Peizhang, Huang Tao, Zhao Shutong, Zhu Yinong, Huang Dingxun, Chen Jingsheng, Han Yougang, Ge Tianhao, Qin Bangzhen, and Xu Shanxiang, have been hired as staff members. The Liaison Group's office is located in the Industry and Commerce Visiting Bureau, and it has been actively operating since yesterday.

▲The Municipal Government Decides on Measures

The Shanghai Municipal Government, in view of the current severe disaster situation in various places and the plight of the people, and with the establishment of the Central Disaster Relief Committee and the Shanghai Fundraising for Provincial Flood Relief Emergency Association in this city, but fearing that fundraising alone may not be sufficient given the vastness of the disaster area and the large number of victims, Mayor Zhang proposed five measures for flood relief at yesterday's municipal government meeting, which were discussed in detail and resolved as follows: (1) To provide as much guidance and assistance as possible to the provincial flood relief emergency associations organized in this city, in order to achieve the goal of raising as much funds as possible for adequate relief. (2) The Social Affairs, Public Safety, and Health Bureaus shall properly plan for the accommodation of refugees. (3) The Finance Bureau shall allocate 100,000 yuan to be used as disaster relief funds, with the usage to be determined on a case-by-case basis. (4) In addition to donating part of their salaries to aid relief, the staff of the Municipal Government's various offices and affiliated institutions shall also be responsible for finding ways to solicit donations. The donation of part of their salaries shall be in accordance with the following standards: (1) Those with monthly salaries below 50 yuan may donate as they wish. (2) Those with salaries between 51 and 100 yuan shall donate at least 5%. (3) Those with salaries between 101 and 200 yuan shall donate at least 10%. (4) Those with salaries between 201 and 300 yuan shall donate at least 20%. (5) Those with salaries between 301 and 400 yuan shall donate at least 30%. (6) Those with salaries between 401 and 500 yuan shall donate at least 40%. (7) Those with salaries above 501 yuan shall donate at least 50%. In addition to donating funds to aid relief in accordance with the above standards, all staff members may also donate clothing and other items and organize disaster relief campaigns to promote publicity and facilitate relief efforts. It is reported that the above measures have been communicated by Mayor Zhang to the Secretariat and various bureaus for prompt implementation. It is also reported that in addition to initially donating one month's salary to aid relief, Mayor Zhang has scheduled to present several measures to the standing committee members, finance committee members, design committee members, and the chief secretary of the city's Fundraising for Provincial Flood Relief Emergency Association on Tuesday, the 25th of this month, to jointly discuss implementation.

▲Social Affairs Bureau Prepares for Accommodation

The Municipal Government, in view of the wide scope and severity of the floods in various provinces and the displacement of the people, and also recognizing the increasing number of disaster victims coming to Shanghai, urgently needs to find ways to accommodate them to prevent homelessness. It is currently planning to allocate a large sum of money and has tasked the Social Affairs, Public Safety, and Health Bureaus with responsible management. On the Social Affairs Bureau's side, it is reported that a temporary relief section has already been established yesterday to facilitate communication and preliminary planning for accommodation matters. It has been scheduled to convene a meeting at the bureau at 10:00 AM on the 24th of this month, inviting representatives from the Public Safety and Health Bureaus, the Shanghai Fundraising for Provincial Flood Relief Emergency Association, the Jiangsu Flood Relief Association, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Charitable Organizations Joint Association, the Guilds Joint Association, the Shanghai Buddhist Association, the Hu Nan Charity Association, the Shanghai Charity Group, the Pu Shan Villa, the Lianyi Charity Association, the Chinese Jishēng Society, the Zhabei Charity Group, the Moral Society, the Shengde Charity Society, the Renji Charity Hall, the Ciyou Xiejihui, the National Medicine Association, the Shanghai Hospital, the Guangyi Chinese Medicine Hospital, the Shenzhou Hospital, the Bean and Rice Industry Guild, the Miscellaneous Grain Industry Guild, the Flour Mill Industry Guild, and the Confectionery and Biscuit Factory Industry Guild to jointly discuss specific measures.

▲Women's Circles Organize Women's Disaster Relief Committee

Since the establishment of the National Government's Flood Relief Committee, the government has specially appointed five people, including Song Ziwen, as committee members, and has also hired dozens of other committee members to expand fundraising. Mrs. Kong Song Ailing, Mrs. Zhang Yu Fengzhi, and others from the women's circles have also been hired as committee members. Mrs. Kong, witnessing the vast disaster area and the urgent need for relief, took advantage of Mrs. Zhang's presence before her return north to convene a meeting yesterday at her residence on Avenue Haig to plan for the implementation of women's disaster relief work. Mrs. Sun Song Qingling, Mrs. Jiang Song Meiling, Mrs. Wang Chonghui, Mrs. Yang Zhaoyun, Mrs. Zhang, the mayor's wife, and Dr. Zheng Yuxiu, among others, attended. As a result of the discussion, a Women's Disaster Relief Committee was organized, and the National Goods Bank was designated as the association's headquarters. However, Mrs. Kong is currently in poor health due to excessive grief over the passing of her mother, and doctors have advised her to avoid strenuous activities. However, Mrs. Kong, recognizing the severity of the disaster, is determined to serve the public despite her illness. Mrs. Zhang, after returning north, will immediately organize the North China Women's Disaster Relief Association and transport grain from Shandong Province to the disaster area for relief distribution.

▲Jointly Discussing Health Measures for Disaster Victims

Yesterday, Dr. Wu Liande, Director of the Seaport Quarantine Station, Hu Hongji, Director of the Health Bureau, and personnel from the Public Concession and French Concession's Public Works Departments, in view of the vast floods in Hankou and the daily arrival of disaster victims in Shanghai in large numbers, which would be difficult to manage properly, and considering that this not only relates to local security but is also particularly important in terms of hygiene, decided to hold a meeting every Friday to jointly plan for prevention and relief measures. At yesterday's first meeting, it was resolved that (1) personnel should be dispatched to Nanjing in advance to establish the first line of epidemic prevention, and that in addition to administering vaccinations when ships pass Xiaguan, the Nanjing municipal authorities should be requested to designate open space for the accommodation of refugees; (2) strict quarantine procedures should be implemented when ships arrive at the Shanghai docks; (3) Mayor Zhang should be requested to designate a place to accommodate disaster victims. The points to be noted for disaster victims are dysentery, cholera, and typhoid fever, the three types of infectious diseases that are unavoidable in flood-affected areas. Therefore, in addition to raising funds for disaster victims, it is urgent to prevent the entry of infectious diseases, which is a crucial task.

▲National Medicine Association Encourages Urgent Relief

The National Medicine Association held a temporary executive and supervisory committee meeting and a joint meeting of the board of directors of the association's affiliated Chinese Medical College at 8:00 PM the night before last. Ding Zhongying, Jiang Wenfang, Xue Wenyuan, Guo Boliang, Huang Baozhong, Fu Yongyan, Qin Bowei, Xie Liheng, Bao Shisheng, Tang Liangchen, Shen Xinjiu, Shen Jianhou, Zhang Zanchen, and two or thirty other people attended. Xie Liheng and Bao Shisheng were publicly elected as chairmen, and Jiang Wenfang reported and recorded the proceedings. (A) Reports: (1) A letter from the Hankou Municipal National Medicine Branch; (2) A letter from the Pudong Branch Office of this association; (3) A letter from Bao Shisheng, President of the Chinese Medical College. (B) Proposals: (1) Ding Zhongying and Guo Boliang proposed that in view of the severe floods in various provinces and the urgent need for relief, should this association do its best to assist? It was resolved that (1) a notice should be published in the newspaper to inform the national medicine community to donate as much as possible, and relief funds should be sent directly to the collection point of the city's Fundraising for Provincial Flood Relief Emergency Association, such as the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, the Central Bank, the China Fú Bank, and the Jin City Bank; (2) when flood relief bonds are issued, this association will do its best to encourage subscriptions; (3) this association will print 500,000 copies of a text encouraging donations for flood relief and distribute them to members to pass on to patients to donate as much as possible; (4) we earnestly request that the national medical and pharmaceutical communities, based on the principle of disaster relief and compassion, jointly take responsibility and proceed in a unified manner. (2) President Bao of the Chinese Medical College proposed to hire Mr. Qin Bowei as the director of education of the college. It was resolved that the proposal was passed. The meeting adjourned at 11:00 PM.

▲Relief Committee Issues a Summary of Governance Regarding the Huai River

The National Government's Flood Relief Committee issued the following summary regarding relief for the floods in the Huai River basin: (1) Affected Areas: The disaster area in the Huai River basin can be divided into two major parts: (A) The upper reaches are west of Yanggānhé and Sānhéjiān, extending upstream to the Pinghan Railway line and the tributaries of the Huai River in northern Anhui, such as the areas along the Sha, Ying, Ru, and Hong Rivers. The floods were caused by mountain torrents, and more than twenty counties were affected. Although the water level has gradually receded, the areas where fields and cities were flooded during the peak of the floods were severely affected. (B) The middle and lower reaches are east of Zhengyangguan on the main stream of the Huai River, passing through Hongze Lake and reaching the downstream river area. The terrain is low-lying, and the current floodwater is submerged to a depth of more than ten feet, and even the shallow areas are two or three feet deep. The area covers approximately 80,000 square miles. In addition to the fields and cities being submerged, there is no hope for the autumn harvest. Therefore, the disaster is more severe than in the upper reaches. Other rivers, such as the Yi and Shu Rivers in Shandong, are also tributaries of the lower reaches of the Huai River, and more than ten counties have also reported floods. Therefore, within the Huai River basin, the disaster area spans the four provinces of Henan, Anhui, Jiangsu, and Shandong, affecting more than eighty counties and approximately ten million disaster victims. (2) Causes of the Disaster: The amount of rainfall in the Huai River basin this year is unprecedented. From late June to early July, there was continuous rain day and night in various places, especially in the high areas of the northwest of the Huai River basin and the tributaries. As a result, mountain torrents erupted and rivers overflowed, and the counties in the Huai River basin in Henan and Anhui and their tributaries were the first to suffer. Subsequently, the floodwater from the upper reaches flowed into the main river, overflowing the banks. From July 11th to 15th, the dikes below Zhengyangguan to Wuhe were first overflowing and then breached, and the dikes along four to five hundred miles were almost completely destroyed. As a result, the main and tributary rivers were connected, and land and water were connected, turning flatlands into lakes. The counties along the Huai River in Anhui suffered the pain of submersion, with no one spared. The Huai River in Henan and Anhui flows to Hongze Lake, which is located at the border of Jiangsu and Anhui, as a temporary destination, and then exits through Gaoyou and Shaobo Lakes to the Yangtze River. The current discharge of large amounts of floodwater at the Yangtze River outlet is insufficient. However, since the water flow from the upper reaches has overflowed the flatlands, the downstream flow is slower. When the disasters in Henan and Anhui were evident, Jiangsu Province, except for the areas along the lake, had not yet suffered a major disaster. By late July, due to the difference between the amount of inflow and outflow each day, the amount of water stored in the lakes increased, and the water level of the lakes continued to rise. The downstream canal is connected to Gaobao Lakes, and the water level of the canal also increased in the same way. Soon, from Huaiyin to Shaobo for three hundred miles, the eastern dike of the canal was in danger of overflowing. Although the Jiangsu Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau and the troops stationed along the Huai River continuously reinforced and raised the dikes, the water level continued to rise, and the danger of the canal dike was indescribable. In early August, three dams of the returning sea dam were opened as a last resort. Since there were no large channels to accommodate the discharge below the dam, and the Fan Gong dike was blocking the way, the water flowing eastward flooded the plains, and the counties in the downstream river area of Jiangsu Province became a swamp. This is a summary of the causes of the disaster in the Huai River basin this year. (3) Work Relief and Disaster Relief: The fundamental plan for treating the flood disaster in the Huai River is: (A) Downstream Tail Water Engineering: The waterway entering the Yangtze River should be reorganized, and a waterway entering the sea should be opened to increase the amount of water discharged into the Yangtze River and the sea. (B) Midstream Flood Control Engineering: Dikes should be built and river channels should be dredged to accommodate flood flows. (C) Upstream Water Storage Engineering: Reservoirs should be built and ditches should be widely opened to store flood flows. The Huai River Guidance Committee has either completed the design of these projects or is actively planning them and will implement them in sequence. Now that a major disaster is at hand, it is imperative to provide disaster relief to the refugees. Work relief is a way to kill two birds with one stone. The principles of work relief must be that the work is something that everyone can do, something that can be done nearby, and something that provides permanent benefits. Therefore, in terms of the Huai River guidance project, the most appropriate projects are the opening of the waterway entering the sea and the construction of dikes on the Huai River in Anhui. All plans have been prepared and can be started in sequence, and the disaster victims in the Huai River basin can be fully utilized.

▲Salt Reclamation Companies Request Dispatch of Personnel to Inspect

The Joint Association of Salt Reclamation Companies in southern Huai River sent a telegram to the Construction Department of the Provincial Government: "To Provincial Government Chairman Ye and Construction Department Director Sun: The heavens have sent a flood disaster, and the people's livelihood is miserable. Who with blood and qi would not be heartbroken? This is the day when the government and the people are jointly planning to provide relief and seek fundamental solutions. If, because of the height of the terrain, we hate each other, trying to save ourselves by cutting off the lives of others, it does not seem to be in accordance with humanity. The salt reclamation companies of the association are located at the edge of the sea tide and usually serve as an outer defense for the upper section of the land, preventing the qi from approaching the people's fields and eliminating the need for tidal defenses. This is also due to the terrain. The companies dare not take credit from the inland. Now, due to the heavy rains in the west and the flooding of the canal, we are in danger. We have already opened the dam for emergency relief to alleviate the disaster in the downstream river area. However, we cannot ignore the lives of the people west of the canal. The dams that can be opened have already been opened. Now, those who hold the position in the downstream river area, because they cannot prevent the canal from opening the dam, are taking their anger out on the salt reclamation companies, saying that we are blocking the flow of water to the sea. If we are removed, they will be happy. How can they know that after the canal dam is opened, the water in the downstream river area is still lower than the eastern salt reclamation area? Since ancient times, the lower river area has been shaped like the bottom of a pot, with the canal high to the west and the peak high to the east. This was not caused by the salt reclamation companies building dams. If we advocate opening more rivers into the sea within the salt reclamation area to facilitate drainage, this is what the companies are seeking, and we have no reason to refuse. If we must remove the embankments and dams, allowing the water to flow on the ground and restoring the ancient wilderness, and then say that it does not obstruct the interior, then may we ask if it is the responsibility of the country to promote prosperity and eliminate harm, so that high and low areas can have harvests? If the higher land is harmed by water later, should we remove it to vent our anger? Then the canal carries water and flows at a high place, and there is always the danger of flooding downstream. How should the hatred be? Can we remove everything west of the canal? Now, those who accuse the salt reclamation companies are speaking recklessly and inciting each other, and we are deeply afraid of causing riots and endless disasters. We respectfully request that you quickly send specialized water conservancy personnel to investigate the truth, announce the correct theory, stop the chaos, and save the imminent disaster. We await your orders with great urgency."

▲Di Chuqing Requests Opening of the Sanmao You River

Di Chuqing sent a telegram to the Provincial Government requesting the opening of the Sanmao You River to discharge water and alleviate the disaster: "To Provincial Government Chairman Ye: With the opening of the sea dam in Jiangbei, several counties in the downstream river area have become swamps. The Dafeng Yuhua Dike is blocking the flow. We earnestly request you to quickly open the Sanmao You River to discharge water and save millions of lives. Di Chuqing bows in respect."

It is not only a matter of benefiting tens of thousands of people for generations to come, but also a source of inspiration. I know that a cup of water cannot extinguish a burning cart of firewood, but Mount Tai and the sea may not be without a trickle of soil and streams. I feel that the people of Hankou are standing in the water, and their cries for help are especially urgent. I cannot sit idly by and have specially donated 3,000 yuan. Please quickly distribute it to the area for urgent relief, hoping to help them reach the other shore.

Anti-Japanese Association Announces Raw Material Passage Measures

▲Industrial and Commercial Circles Express Cooperation and Mutual Progress

▲Five-Year Plan First Determines Drafting Steps

The Anti-Japanese and Aid-Overseas Chinese Committee has been working on the resistance-to-goods movement for days and is still in progress. After the various labor unions resolved to express their dissent regarding merchants conducting self-inspection, the leaders of the industrial and commercial circles explained in detail, and after the opinions were communicated, it was realized that the methods of both parties were originally different. They still expressed the spirit of cooperation and mutual progress. All misunderstandings have been completely eliminated. The passage measures for essential industrial raw materials have also been publicly announced yesterday. The five-year industrial plan first determines the drafting steps. The various news reports are recorded separately as follows:

▲Raw Material Essential Goods Passage Measures The Anti-Japanese Association issued a public announcement yesterday, stating: "After investigation, the passage measures for essential industrial raw materials have been resolved at the 11th Standing Committee meeting of this association and will be implemented from the 20th of this month. The measures are hereby publicly announced for your information." The attached measures are as follows: (1) Those who purchase Japanese industrial raw materials and essential goods must first apply for registration with the registration section of this association. (2) After registration, if this association verifies that there are no goods from other countries that can be substituted, permission will be granted to draw a fund to establish a factory. (3) After approval to establish a factory, a fund should be deposited at the bank designated by this association. (4) This association will issue a passage permit based on the bank's deposit receipt, allowing passage. (5) The articles of association, general rules, triplicate deposit slip, and passage permit forms for establishing a factory will be determined separately.

▲Five-Year Plan Determines Drafting Steps, The five-year industrial plan, since the Design Committee of the association resolved to appoint economic experts Li Quanshi, Xu Yongzuo, and Gui Yanfang to draft it, after two meetings of the association, has been slightly discussed, but no concrete measures have been seen to be expressed to the outside world. According to Mr. Yan Guangqian, private secretary of the Design Committee, speaking to the New Voice News reporter, the five-year industrial plan takes the overall development of China as a premise and is greatly related to the future. Observing the Soviet Union's five-year plan has had a profound impact on the international community. However, the Soviet Union's plan, with the power of the government, gathered talents from all over the country and devoted themselves to planning, so that this effect was achieved. Now, our country intends to proudly draft a five-year industrial plan, and it will not be successful unless experts are gathered together for joint research. The drafters also think the same way. Therefore, they only intend to stipulate the steps on how to draft it and submit written opinions for joint discussion at the Design Committee meeting next Monday to proceed with the process.

▲Expressions from Jiangyin and Wuxian Telegrams (1) Jiangyin Telegram: Shanghai Anti-Japanese and Aid-Overseas Chinese Committee, Greetings. Our association was established at the Qi Day (8th) meeting and has been telegraphed on record. After investigation, the first committee meeting was of the unanimous opinion that Shanghai is the throat for the import of foreign goods, and Japanese goods in the interior are all imported from Shanghai. If Shanghai can thoroughly inspect and eliminate them, then there will be no problem in the interior. We should telegraph your association to urge strict inspection to eliminate the source and prevent Japanese goods from flowing into the interior, etc. The minutes of the resolution are on file. A corresponding record telegram is hereby sent, hoping you will investigate and implement it vigorously. Deeply grateful. Jiangyin Economic Severance Committee for Japan, Knocking, Seal. (2) Wuxian Telegram: Shanghai Municipal Anti-Japanese and Aid-Overseas Chinese Committee, Greetings. I have recently read in the newspapers that your association has seized Japanese goods, and Japanese soldiers have forcibly seized goods, arrested staff, and committed illegal acts of insults, which are outrageous. We have already telegraphed the National Government to order the Executive Yuan to order the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to conduct serious negotiations with Japan. We also send a special telegram of condolences, hoping that you will continue to fight. Our association vows to be your backing. The telegram is urgent and pressing, and we are extremely grateful. Wuxian Anti-Japanese and Aid-Overseas Chinese Committee Chairman Zhang Wentang, Fan Junbo, Lu Baoyu, Knocking.

Minutes of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's Anti-Japanese Goods Research Meeting

▲Publicly Announce to All Circles to Expose Unscrupulous Merchants as Much as Possible

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce's Anti-Japanese Goods Research Committee held its second standing committee meeting yesterday. The attending committee members were Zheng Chengqing, Ye Chunciao, Ye Jiaxing, Zheng Zenan, Fu Zuoheng, etc. Zheng Chengqing chaired, Jin Shengbai recorded. The resolutions are as follows: (1) The Hardware Industry Association sent a letter requesting discussion on how to handle cases where the designated Japanese goods cannot be returned. Resolution: It should be handled in accordance with the Anti-Japanese Association's resolution on sacrificing the deposit. (2) The Transshipment Association sent a letter requesting discussion on how to handle cases where non-Japanese goods are transported by Japanese ships, or where only Japanese ships operate. Resolution: It should be handled in accordance with the Anti-Japanese Association's resolution that "in places where other ships operate, every effort should be made to avoid transporting by Japanese ships; in places where no other ships operate, temporary accommodation should be provided." (3) A letter from the　Country suggesting ten anti-Japanese measures. Resolution: File. (4) Wu Yizhi sent a letter requesting research on long-term anti-Japanese measures. Resolution: File. (5) The Transportation Industry Association sent a letter requesting discussion on how to handle Japanese goods that were previously received for transport but have been delayed and not yet unloaded, during the current anti-Japanese period. Resolution: It should be handled in accordance with the measures stipulated by the Anti-Japanese Association. (6) The Ginseng and Bird's Nest Industry Association sent a letter stating that the sealed goods have been stored for a long time and may become moldy. Please discuss methods to provide relief to maintain capital. Reply letter: Move the goods and unpack them first for sunning and treatment. (7) The daily necessities group and industrial raw materials group's working committee resolved that the four relief methods proposed by the calico bleaching and dyeing industry association should be approved and implemented. Resolution: Handle it in accordance with the research and decision methods and send a letter to the association. (8) The method for collecting industrial funds has been resolved and submitted to groups (3) and (4) for research. A meeting of the two groups should be convened on a regular basis to discuss the progress. Resolution: A joint meeting of the two groups will be convened next Wednesday. (9) Discuss whether economic severance with Japan should not tend to Japanese ships, which is in line with the principle. Resolution: Publicly announce to all circles. (10) Discuss how to crack down on unscrupulous merchants who still import Japanese goods privately after the Anti-Japanese Association's operations. Resolution: Publish an announcement in the newspaper to publicly announce to all circles to expose as much as possible.

Female Student Commits Suicide by Drowning

▲Sacrificing Her Life for Patriotism

▲Hoping Six Items Will Awaken the Chinese People

At 10:00 AM yesterday, on the Pu shore in front of the Naval Hospital on Zhang Xuehua Beach in Wusong, a person dressed in a white silk cheongsam, resembling a female student, suddenly committed suicide by drowning. Before entering the water, she discarded several books she was holding on the beach. Then, she calmly walked towards the Huangpu River and jumped in. At that time, the Junpu Bureau's Li Hua small steamer was towing a barge and several mechanics were going to the old Hailong dredging machine ship for repairs. Passing by the area, they caught sight of a woman drowning. The helmsman, Lu Hongsheng, immediately steered the rudder to rescue her. However, the distance was too far, and towing a large barge slowed down the small steamer, so it was too late to catch up, and the female student tragically drowned. Later, the small steamer approached the beach and picked up the books discarded by the woman. One of them was a blue-grid, green-covered practice book with Chinese and Western circular seals on the cover. The Chinese characters said "Nanyang Girls' High School" and there were handwritten words in fountain pen "Tang Deling's friend's address," etc. It is not known whether the woman was Tang Deling or whether there was another Tang Deling. Therefore, it is specially recorded for those who are familiar with her to investigate. The addresses, house numbers, and names of many friends in Tianjin, Hankou, and this port are written in the book, including Li Hui at 30 Defuli, Chuan Highway, Baotong Road, Zhabei, Li Shenrou at 1020 North Fifth Lane, Hengqingli, Qipulu, and Lu Tongsun at 4 Yideli, Tiantong'an Road, Zhabei, and Sun Jingyan at 3 Tiandeli, Tongji Road. However, there was another piece of paper on which was written "Patriotic Chain," the words were as follows:

Comrades, do you read the newspaper? Haven't you seen the Koreans brutally killing our overseas Chinese compatriots? We must know who is directing it. Isn't it the Japanese dwarfs who created the May 30th Incident? Since you are Chinese, then you should be determined to: (1) Overthrow imperialism. (2) Do not help the Japanese do things. (3) Do not buy any Japanese clothing, food, housing, or other utensils. (4) Do not supply the Japanese with any goods. (5) Forever sever economic ties with the Japanese. (6) Promote domestic goods. Comrades, after receiving this letter, you must fulfill your patriotic methods and please sacrifice some time within 24 hours of receiving the letter to transcribe nine copies and send them to your classmates and friends for widespread publicity. Friends, if you buy even a little Japanese goods, do not fulfill the above items, and do not forward the nine copies of the patriotic chain, then I will unceremoniously call you a slave to a fallen nation, a cold-blooded animal. According to superstition, your family will be childless, your family will be ruined, and your family will be destroyed. Friends, do you hate me? Do you scold me? Sincerely, a patriotic comrade who knows you.

From this, it is undoubtedly clear that the female student's suicide was due to her keen patriotism and her anger over the brutal killing of overseas Chinese compatriots by the Japanese. Although suicide is not desirable, her ambition is also worthy of pity.

Worker Wrongly Accused of Theft and Beaten, Angered and Poisoned Himself to Death

▲The Deceased's Aftermath is Extremely Desolate

▲The Perpetrators Still Attempt to Shirk Responsibility

On the morning of the 13th of this month, at 11:00 AM, in the Tao Rongji Construction Factory on Liaoyang Road, the night watchman Lao Shaoxing, also known as Chen Qingliang, 34 years old, was involved in the theft of one dan of rice and two boxes of nails from the factory. He was tied up and beaten by his colleagues, and then released. Chen felt wronged and secretly swallowed opium, which caused him to be sent to the hospital. He died despite treatment. The various circumstances have been reported in previous newspapers. The Chinese and Western detectives of the Huishan Police Station have successively arrested the perpetrators Wang Xuquan from Pudong, Lu Xuxu, Lu Xiusheng, Shen Maojian, Song Afu from Wusong, and Li Yuanhai from Haimen, and sent them to the First Special Court for questioning and detention. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xieqiu opened the court for continued questioning. According to the statement of Li Zhishan, the lawyer of the police station, and the statement of Wu Chenshi, the younger brother of the deceased Chen Qingliang, whose original home was in Jin, had a 69-year-old mother, a wife, a 7-year-old daughter, and a 3-year-old son. He heard that he was a small worker in the factory, earning eight yuan a month, had no hobbies, and had no illnesses. At that time, he swallowed opium without knowing it. Now he demands that the perpetrators be severely punished. Wang Xuquan firmly claimed that the stolen rice and nails belonged to Lu Xiusheng, the head of the carpentry team, who asked him and Lu Xuxu to keep them. The deceased stole them, and Lu asked him to tie him up and question him, but he did not beat him. Lu Xuxu claimed that he was not instructed by Lu Xiusheng to tie him up, but that it was the idea of him and Wang Xuquan. He did not beat him either. Lu Xiusheng confessed that he was not present when Lao Shaoxing (i.e., the deceased) was tied up. Later, he saw someone tying him up, but he did not know who. He also hired lawyer Wu Linkun to defend him. Shen Maojian and Song Afu confessed that they were carpenters in the factory and had nothing to do with the tying up and beating of the deceased at the time. They asked for leniency. Li Yuanhai confessed that he and Lao Shaoxing were both small workers. He was not present when he was tied up. Because he accused him of stealing the rice and nails with him, he used an iron bar to lightly hit his left foot. Then he was released. Judge Xiao then asked Wang Xuquan and Lu Xuxu whether Shen Maojian and Song Afu participated in the tying up and beating of the deceased at the time. They all claimed that they did not. Then he ordered Shen and Song to be released on bail by a reliable shop, and the rest were detained for further verification at a later date.

Case of Forced Inducement of a Foster Daughter of Judge Xiong Fei

▲ Shen An'nan Appeals Against the Original Sentence

Xiong Fei, a judge of the Civil Execution Division of the First Special District Court, resides at No. 18, Rehe Road. He has two foster daughters, Lai Fu and Lin Xi, both around 19 years old and possessing some beauty. In February of this year (lunar calendar), both girls suddenly disappeared simultaneously. It was reported to the Huizi police station, and after investigation by Detective Xiao Shangwu, it was discovered that Lai Fu had been induced into fornication by Shen An'nan of Ningbo and was hiding in a hotel. Shen and Lai Fu were arrested and taken to the police station, but Lin Xi's whereabouts remain unknown to this day. The next morning, they were escorted to the Special Court. After questioning, Shen An'nan was sentenced to six months in prison. Lai Fu, unwilling to return home, was sent to the Women and Children Relief Association for care. These details were previously reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that Shen, dissatisfied with the sentence, has hired lawyer Shen Xingxia to file an appeal. Yesterday morning, the Criminal Division Chief of the High Court, Song Yuan, along with judges Du and Gao, and Prosecutor Zheng, held a court session for the hearing. Lawyer Zhang Tianyin appeared in court on behalf of the police station to present the case. Subsequently, Judge Song questioned the appellant, Shen An'nan, about his reasons for dissatisfaction. According to Shen, he and Lai Fu became acquainted because they lived nearby. One night in February, Shen encountered Lai Fu at the intersection of North Xizang Road and inquired why she was out so late. Lai Fu claimed that she had escaped due to mistreatment by her mistress and did not want to return. Shen obtained her consent and took her to the Zhongxing Hotel on Avenue Edward VII, later moving to the China South Hotel. They eventually rented a house to live together due to financial constraints, but this was entirely of the girl's own volition and not inducement. Xiong Lai Fu was also sent to court by representatives of the Women and Children Relief Association. According to Lai Fu, she is 19 years old and met Shen in January. She escaped with Lin Xi due to mistreatment by her employer. She is a maid in the Xiong family, not a foster daughter, and has been in the Xiong residence in Jiangxi for ten years before coming to Shanghai. She now wishes to live with Shen and does not want to return. Judge Song verified the testimony and ordered the commencement of arguments. Lawyer Shen Xingxia, representing the appellant, argued that the original judgment was based on Article 257 of the Criminal Law, which punishes those who induce or abduct men or women under the age of 20 to leave the guardianship of their parents, guardians, or curators. However, Lai Fu is a maid in the Xiong Deng family, referring to Xiong Deng as "Madam." Does Xiong Deng have the right to guardianship and prosecution? Furthermore, according to Lai Fu's testimony, there is another girl named Lin Xi in the Xiong family. If they were foster daughters, one would have been sufficient; why would they need two? Moreover, the name "Lai Fu" clearly indicates that she is a servant girl. Therefore, Xiong Deng has no right to prosecute, and the original judgment should be revoked, declaring the appellant not guilty. Lawyer Zhang Tianyin then rose to respond, stating that the original trial record clearly stated that Xiong Lai Fu was indeed a foster daughter, not a servant girl. Shen's lawyer claims that because there are two girls, Lai Fu and Lin Xi, in the Xiong residence, they must be maids. This is unreasonable. Famous Shanghai figure Hartung has countless adopted sons and daughters. The name "Lai Fu" cannot be used to assume that she is a servant. The appeal should be rejected, and the original judgment upheld. Judge Song verified the testimony and ordered the case to be adjourned for further hearing. Shen An'nan was remanded in custody.

Jiangnan Shipbuilding Factory Sues Russian for Losses

▲ Chartering Vessel but Failing to Take Delivery as Agreed

▲ No Rental Payments Received

The Jiangnan Shipbuilding Factory of the Navy has recently engaged lawyer Qiu Fenling to file a lawsuit with the First Special District Court, accusing Russian national Qiu Niheng (Chanechen, owner of the Shanghai Salvage Company) of breach of contract and demanding compensation for losses. The complaint states that the plaintiff entered into a charter agreement for the Hua'an vessel with the defendant on June 1 of this year. According to Article 13 of the contract, the charter fee was 12,000 yuan per month, calculated from the date the vessel was repaired and delivered. A check for 12,000 yuan, dated June 30, was received from the defendant on June 26, but it was not honored on the due date. By that time, the plaintiff had already completed the repair of the Hua'an vessel and was prepared to deliver it on July 4, and the defendant was formally notified to take delivery. However, the defendant not only failed to pay the charter fee as agreed but also failed to take delivery of the vessel. On July 17, the defendant issued another note, extending the payment of the 12,000 yuan charter fee to July 25, promising to compensate for all losses in case of default. However, the defendant again failed to meet the deadline. Since the Hua'an vessel was chartered by the defendant, the plaintiff notified them to prepare for delivery, and the defendant should have immediately taken delivery and paid the charter fee as agreed. The defendant's failure to take delivery constitutes a breach of contract, which is entirely their own fault. The plaintiff cannot be expected to suffer losses without cause. The court is requested to order the defendant to return the check for 12,000 yuan (prepaid rent) and pay cash, as well as to be responsible for the loss of 12,000 yuan per month from August 4 until the vessel is chartered out again, and legal interest from July 4 until the date of execution, and to bear the costs of this lawsuit. Yesterday morning, Judge Guo Shouyi held a hearing to summon the parties. The defendant's lawyer requested a postponement, stating that they had just been appointed and had not had time to prepare. Chen Zaofan, representing the Jiangnan Shipbuilding Factory, recounted the circumstances of the case. Judge Guo then adjourned the hearing for a later date.

Master Killed by Pet Tiger Cat

▲ Wang Jingcai Loved His Cat, But Was Bitten to Death

Wang Jingcai, a native of Jingjiang residing at No. 124, Yaoshui Lane, Xiaoshadu, West Shanghai, kept a large male tiger cat. It was incredibly agile at catching rats, and the owner loved it. However, a few days ago (the 18th), the cat's behavior changed. It ate less. The owner thought it was sick and bought Wuyao (Lindera root) to mix with its food. (It is said that Wuyao can cure cat illnesses.) However, after eating it, the cat fiercely bit the owner several times. At the time, he only felt unbearable pain. Several days later, Wang experienced severe itching and pain at the bite site and began foaming at the mouth. In an instant, Wang lost consciousness and rolled and crawled on the ground. His family immediately hired a car to take Wang to the Labor Hospital for treatment. However, he died en route before reaching the hospital. It is truly strange.

Inside Story of Gunfire and Resisting Arrest in West Shanghai

▲ The Reason Was a Conspiracy to Rob Land

Gang policemen Deng Zhiming and Zhang Jinshan, leading Du Futang and others from the Third Branch of the Sixth District of the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, were on duty at Caoxi Road around 4 a.m. the day before yesterday when they saw a white-plate operating car with the city license number 4429 carrying four people, heading south from the north. Because it was late at night, their behavior was suspicious, so they immediately ordered the car to stop for inspection. Two passengers got out of the car and were searched, and no illegal items were found. When the third person got out, unexpectedly, he pulled out a gun and fired at the police, firing several shots. The police also drew their guns and returned fire, and the car immediately turned around and fled. The three people who got out of the car also fled in different directions. This was briefly reported in yesterday's newspaper. It has now been learned that the criminals were indeed conspiring to rob land in the countryside. Earlier, Mao Caichen, a farmer residing at No. 17, Maojia Catholic Church, West Caohijing Town, learned that Mao Songtao next door had a large quantity of opium. On the afternoon of the 19th, he reported to Mao Jiusheng (a mason, 22 years old) in his clan on Rue Gascogne in the French Concession.

They agreed to go rob the opium that night. After receiving the message, Jiusheng invited Xie Amao, Xu Guansheng, Lao San, and four others. At around 3 a.m. on the 20th, they went to the Dade Motor Company at No. 1194 Route Lafayette and rented a covered car with the city license number 4429, driven by Feng Aqi, and sped to Dexi Road. They were inspected by the gang policemen and fired shots to escape. Xie Amao, sitting in the front of the car, forced Feng Aqi to drive away. Helplessly, Feng drove back to the concession and reported to the Lujiiawan Police Station. After a brief interrogation by the police chief, it was decided that the case occurred in the interior, so Detective Li Yaolong, Tang Hao, and others were sent to the Sixth District Third Branch, along with Xie Amao and the car driver Feng Aqi, and the car No. 4429, for investigation. At the same time, Zhou Yida, the police chief of the Tushanwan Police Station of the Sixth District Second Branch, also heard gunshots and police sirens and led the police to search the area. Mao Jiusheng was apprehended in the riverbank behind the Shunzhi Guild Hall on Tianyaoqiao Road and taken back to the station. After interrogation by Director Liu, he confessed that at around 3 a.m. today, he and his friends Xu Guansheng, Lao San, and Xie Amao went to Mao Songtao's house at Maojia Catholic Church, West Caohijing Town, to rob opium. They had a pistol, and when they encountered the police at Caoxi Road, Xu Guansheng fired the gun directly, and they fled in different directions. Director Liu then sent Patrol Officer Wang Xuce and Liu Shaoqing, the leader of the Sixth District Detective Team, along with Detective Cao Chuqiao, Patrol Officer Fu Xingen of the Third Branch, and Police Chief Man Qiwei, to search Mao Songtao's house at the Catholic Church with Mao Jiusheng. However, Mao had also fled beforehand, and there was no opium in the house. Mao Caichen, who sent the message, was also apprehended. After separate and strict interrogation by Director Liu, all the defendants admitted to the robbery. The gun belonged to Xu Guansheng, and he was the one who fired it. After obtaining the confession, Director Liu temporarily released Feng Aqi and ordered the police to strictly apprehend the three fugitives: Xu Guansheng, Lao San, and Mao Songtao, who sold the opium, for investigation. Mao Jiusheng, Xie Amao, and Mao Caichen were all sent to the bureau for strict punishment according to the law.

Scene of Star Company Colleagues Welcoming at the Dock

Zhang and Zhou first boarded a small motorboat to talk to them on the ship and then came ashore together. A camera was placed on the dock, and a white banner reading "Welcome Mr. Hong Shen and Mr. Garson from America to Shanghai" was hung high. At that time, the welcomers surrounded Mr. Hong and others as they disembarked from the ship. The cameraman moved the camera to record the scene on film. The accompanying Westerners included Mr. Harry Garson and technicians, along with their families, totaling fifteen people. After warmly greeting everyone, they boarded cars and drove to the company on Route Doumer. A large amount of equipment had not yet been unloaded. In addition to reporters from Chinese and Western newspapers, Zhou Shihun, editor of "Movie Monthly," Xu Jinzhi of "Wen Hua Monthly," and Tang Bihua of "Movie Life Society" all brought cameras and took many news photos.

Wu Gunong Covered in Excrement

▲ Qingpu Doctor Arrives to Diagnose Dead Pulse

▲ Police Station Doesn't Handle Legal Matters

Wu Gunong, a pediatric specialist from Qingpu, has been making a decent living with his ancestral skills. However, he is inherently slow, so his house calls are usually in the middle of the night, neglecting the patients. Hence, he has the nickname "Muddlehead." Recently, Zhang Qixiang, the manager of the Xiangtai Xin dry goods store in Hongkou, took his sick child to the store for convenience and specifically hired Wu to treat him. However, by the time Doctor Wu arrived in Shanghai, his child had already been dead for several hours. Zhang, grief-stricken, thought that Doctor Wu treated human life like grass, completely delaying the treatment. However, he still treated Doctor Wu cordially, inviting him upstairs to examine the child. Zhang had Doctor Wu take the dead child's pulse. Wu, realizing something was wrong, hurriedly tried to escape, but one of the store's apprentices threw the pre-arranged excrement at Doctor Wu's face, covering his head with it. The stench was unbearable. Doctor Wu's servant, who had come with him, immediately shouted for the police, and they were all taken to the Harbin Police Station for investigation. After questioning by the police chief, it was decided that this case was within the scope of the law and should be prosecuted in court, not under the jurisdiction of the police station. It is said that Doctor Wu intends to file a formal lawsuit.

Unforeseen Disaster While Driving for Pleasure

▲ Seven People, Including Men, Women, the Elderly, and Children, Injured

▲ Good Fortune and Misfortune Depend on Each Other; It's Best to Be Content

Yesterday morning, at around 5 a.m., seven people, including men, women, the elderly, and children, suddenly arrived at the Herde Motor Company at No. A-1709 Avenue Edward VII, claiming to rent a car to drive around Wusong. The company's accountant ordered driver Yao Kunsheng to drive a covered car, No. 17573, to their destination. When the car reached the vicinity of Jungong Road, the driver, seeing that the area was desolate and there were few pedestrians, accelerated. He intended to drive to the Wusong seaside, but misfortune is unpredictable, and an accident occurred. Due to excessive speed, the car accidentally hit a large tree on the side of the road while turning on Jungong Road, causing irreparable damage to the machinery. The passengers in the car were all injured. After the police from the Seventh District Public Security Bureau arrived after receiving the report, they first took the driver Yao Kun into custody for investigation. The injured people hired another car and went to the Baolong Hospital for treatment. The names of the injured people are listed as follows: Shi Chendong, 25 years old, Suzhou native, tailor, injured his left forehead; Liu Laoqi, 15 years old, Suzhou native, injured his arms, etc.; Liu Laoliu, 18 years old, female, Suzhou native, injured her face and lips; Liu Zhangyou, a child, 12 years old, Suzhou native, abrasions on his hands; Mao Jinda, male, 22 years old, Suzhou native, beef seller, injured his face; Yan Dalang, male, 38 years old, Chongming native, bamboo craftsman, fractured his left arm; Yang Mingming, male, 24 years old, Suzhou native, minor injuries to the top of his head. After examination by the hospital doctor, those with more serious injuries were admitted to the hospital for treatment, while the rest were treated and bandaged and then discharged from the hospital.

Deserter Who Stole Military Equipment Apprehended

The day before yesterday, around 5 a.m., on the Shanghai-Taicang Motor Road, a large man, about six feet tall or more, wearing a white short-sleeved shirt and white shorts, carrying four rifles on his back and bullets wrapped around his waist, was walking on the Shihe Bridge west of Dachang. He was resting on the bridge. At that time, there were many villagers from the area and two plainclothes security guards on the bridge, enjoying the cool air. Seeing the large man, they asked what he was carrying on his back. The large man replied that they were water pipes (because the guns were wrapped in cloth). They also saw bullets wrapped around his waist, which made them even more suspicious. The large man angrily said, "They are rifles! Do you dare to take them?" As he spoke, he put down the guns and threw them on the bridge, saying, "Do you dare to take them?" After a while, he left. The two guards knew that he was not a good person, so they followed him to see what he was up to. They walked to the vicinity of Maqiao, which is about three miles away from Dachang. The sky was just beginning to brighten. Seeing that he was being followed, the large man loaded the guns with bullets and fired several shots. The guards lay down in the fields to avoid the bullets and fled back to the regiment headquarters to report. They also reported to the Security Office's company, which sent a large number of armed soldiers and guards to arrest him. At that time, the villagers of Maqiao, hearing the gunshots, suspected that there were bandits and started beating gongs and drums, armed with wooden sticks, shoulder poles, etc., and surrounded the area to capture him. The soldiers arrived and also fired back. The large man, seeing that he was outnumbered, threw the guns and bullets into the river and surrendered empty-handed. He was taken back to the company headquarters. At the same time, the abandoned guns and bullets were recovered. After interrogation by the company clerk, he confessed that his name was Chen Fusheng, 26 years old, from Liuhe. He had joined the 5th Mortar Team in Zhabei, Shanghai, on May 7. The guns were stolen from the armory upstairs, lowered down with a rope, so the guards were unaware. He passed through many police checkpoints, and no one interfered. He said that the local people were really formidable, and he would rather die than suffer. After verifying the confession, the company clerk reported to company commander Zhang Xueli, who took a memorial and escorted him to Shanghai by car at 8 a.m. yesterday and then transferred him to the Shanghai-Hangzhou train to be sent to the Songjiang Pacification Command (i.e., the Second Regiment Headquarters of the Jiangsu Security Office) for investigation.

Customs Announces Measures for Inland Goods Transshipment Tax

The Jianghai Customs has stipulated matters concerning the inland goods transshipment tax and officially announced its implementation yesterday. The original text is recorded below. It is now stipulated that all inland goods transshipped from this trading port to another trading port for export to foreign countries, or re-exported to foreign countries, shall be handled in accordance with the following measures from the date of this announcement: (1) (A) For inland goods, including silks, lacquerware, and paper umbrellas, transported to a trading port that should pay the transshipment tax, or transported to foreign countries that should be exempt from the export tax, and declared to be transshipped to foreign countries via other ports, it is now necessary to handle them in accordance with the measures for machine-made goods transported to foreign factories via trading ports. That is, the goods are exempt from tax at the port of origin, but a stamp is affixed to the duplicate manifest, stating that if the goods are not transported to foreign countries within the prescribed transshipment period at the final port, the port will collect the transshipment tax. (B) For the above-mentioned inland goods that have paid the transshipment tax at the original port of shipment and declared that they will be re-exported to foreign countries from the final port within one year, the transshipment tax paid will be refunded by the final port to which the goods are transported to foreign countries upon presentation of the tax payment certificate or export certificate. When the above-mentioned measures are implemented, all guarantee measures for lacquerware and paper umbrellas will be abolished. However, the current guarantee measures for straw hats and straw hat braids, as well as the tax payment measures, will all be handled as before. (2) (A) For inland goods transported to a trading port that should be exempt from the transshipment tax, or transported to foreign countries that should pay the export tax, and declared to be transshipped to foreign countries at the original port of shipment, the export tax should be paid at that port. If the goods are not transshipped to foreign countries at the final port within the prescribed time limit, the port that consumes the goods should check the tax payment certificate or export certificate issued by the original port of shipment, and refund the export tax that has been paid. (B) For the above-mentioned inland goods that have declared at the original port of shipment that they will be re-exported to foreign countries from the final port within one year, the export tax should be paid at that port. If the goods are not re-exported to foreign countries within one year, the port that consumes the goods should check the tax payment certificate or export certificate issued by the original port of shipment, and refund the export tax that has been paid. (3) For taxable inland goods declared to be shipped abroad via other ports, and the export tax has been paid at the original port of shipment, if they are not exported abroad at the final port but are consumed at other ports, the port that consumes the goods should verify the tax payment certificate or export certificate issued by the original port of shipment, and refund or collect the difference between the transshipment tax and the export tax. (4) For taxable inland goods that are not declared for transshipment tax, or re-exported to foreign countries, or are transported domestically and their transshipment tax has been paid at the original port of shipment, if they are subsequently re-exported to foreign countries by other ports within one year of the original document reaching that port, the final port should verify the tax payment certificate or export certificate issued by the original port of shipment, and collect or refund the difference between the export tax and the transshipment tax. The above measures are hereby announced for the information of all merchants.

County Finance Bureau Announces Deadline for Payment of Brokerage Tax

The Shanghai County Finance Bureau issued an announcement yesterday stating, "Brokerage tax is a special fund for education and is related to education expenses. Everyone should actively pay it in turn to fulfill the obligation of taxpayers. It has been found that many brokers in the county do not exchange their licenses on time when they expire. Some brokers even hide and do not comply with the regulations to obtain licenses. They engage in unlicensed brokerage activities, hoping to take advantage of loopholes, and this has become a prevailing practice. Since taking office, the director of this bureau has repeatedly received strict orders from the Education Funding Management Office to rectify the situation and can no longer tolerate concealment and delay. Therefore, this announcement is hereby issued to all brokers in the county for their information. If your brokerage license is about to expire, you must come to the bureau to donate and exchange for a new license within this month when it expires. If you fail to do so, you will be punished according to the regulations. Those who have newly established brokerage firms must also quickly come to the bureau to obtain licenses and start their business, and must not wait and delay the exchange, which may lead to punishment. In addition to dispatching personnel to conduct random inspections at any time, this announcement is hereby issued. Furthermore, the personnel dispatched by this bureau for investigation will be issued investigation brokerage license stamps as proof. Be careful not to be deceived. Please be informed."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Approves Measures for Coordinated Collection and Payment of Business Tax

▲Chamber of Commerce Establishes Office and Forms Committee

▲Industry Associations to Handle Collection for Members

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce held its 18th Executive Committee meeting at 4 PM yesterday. Attendees included Wang Xiaolai, Fang Jiaobo, Pei Yunqing, Lu Fengzhu, Ma Jiliang, Chen Songyuan, Jiang Zhigang, Lu Qisheng, and others. Wang Xiaolai presided over the meeting. After the usual formalities, Secretary Yan E'sheng reported on important correspondence and read the resolutions of the 17th Executive Committee meeting. The committee then discussed and amended the draft measures for the Chamber of Commerce's coordinated collection and payment of business tax, and the draft measures for entrusting industry associations to collect and pay business tax. The original text of the measures is recorded below:

▲Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce Measures for Coordinated Collection and Payment of Business Tax (1) These measures are based on the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax and the regulations for entrusting the Chamber of Commerce with coordinated collection and payment. (2) The Chamber of Commerce will establish a special Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce Office for Coordinated Collection and Payment of Business Tax to handle the coordinated collection and payment of business tax matters. (3) The office will establish a committee that will uphold the intentions of the Standing Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and preside over the office's affairs. (4) The committee will be composed of the following members: (A) One Standing Committee member, (B) Director of the General Affairs Section, (C) Director of the Finance Section, (D) Director of the Commerce Section. The Standing Committee member will serve as the chairman of the committee. (5) The internal organization of the office will be determined separately. (6) For industries that have legally established industry associations, the business tax of that industry should be collected and paid by the office through the industry association. (7) The business tax collected and paid by the industry association should include all businesses in that industry, not limited to association members. (8) For shops in various industries in the city that do not yet have an industry association, their business tax will be collected directly by the office. (9) These measures will be implemented upon approval by the Executive Committee.

▲Also, Measures for Entrusting Industry Associations to Collect Business Tax (1) These measures are based on Article 2 of the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Measures for Entrusting the Chamber of Commerce with Coordinated Collection and Payment. (2) The industry associations referred to in these measures are limited to those that have been officially registered with the Social Affairs Bureau and have paid the Chamber of Commerce's annual membership fee for this year and obtained a membership certificate. (3) The scope of the business tax collected by each industry association is limited to the shops in its industry. The chairman and standing committee members of the association will bear full responsibility. (4) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce will hand over the business tax declaration forms to each industry association, which will distribute them to shops in the same industry. The shops will fill out the forms according to the prescribed format and send them to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for forwarding to the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Collection Office to compile a tax collection list. (5) The collection and reporting of business tax by industry associations should be completely transparent. A monthly report should be prepared and submitted to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for verification. The deadline for submitting the report is no later than the 4th day of the following month. (6) Industry associations should pay the tax collected from shops in the same industry, together with the receipts, to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce Office for Coordinated Collection and Payment of Business Tax before 3 PM every day, for forwarding to the municipal bank. (7) For the convenience of verification, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce may dispatch inspectors to the industry associations to conduct random audits. (8) Business tax collection receipts should be obtained by the industry associations from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. The chairman and standing committee members of the association, together with the inspectors, should verify, fill out, and issue the receipts at any time. (9) The expenses required for industry associations to collect business tax may be allocated at 5% of the tax paid for application. The allocated expenses should be obtained by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce from the Finance Bureau on a monthly basis in accordance with Article 4 of the Municipal Accounting Regulations, and then transferred to the industry associations. They must not be deducted from the tax collected. Regarding the issuance of licenses and tax payment for business operators, and all other matters, they should all be handled in accordance with the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Collection Regulations and various rules and regulations. (10) (1) If a business operator violates the penalty clauses, the industry association should be instructed to report it to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, which will forward it to the Shanghai Municipal Business Tax Collection Office for investigation and handling in accordance with the regulations. (10) (2) If a business operator changes its organization, closes down, or moves, it should report it to the Chamber of Commerce at any time, which will forward it to the Business Tax Collection Office for verification. The same applies to newly established businesses. (10) (3) The business licenses that business operators should obtain will be obtained by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and then handed over to the industry associations for distribution to shops in the same industry. (10) (4) These measures will be implemented upon approval by the Executive Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the same applies to amendments.

Comprehensive Legal Books Published

▲Outline of Commercial Law, On Bankruptcy Law

Wang Junqufei, the current judge of the Shanghai Local Court, has a long career in the legal profession and profound knowledge. Various law schools in Shanghai are competing to hire him. Because there are no comprehensive textbooks available in the market for the subjects taught by Wang Jun, he compiled and printed "On Property Law" and "Outline of Bankruptcy Law" last year, which became popular in the country. It is now heard that he has also written "Outline of Commercial Law" based on his years of experience in commercial law. It discusses in detail the evolution of commercial law in our country, the merits and demerits of commercial law in various countries, and the legal principles of commercial law. The content is rich, and the style is precise. The entire book is about 200,000 words, bound in one volume, and sells for 2.20 yuan. It is currently being bound and will be published within a day or two. At the same time, he felt that the previous compilation of "Outline of Bankruptcy Law" was slightly brief, and scholars might find it difficult to fully understand. Therefore, he also re-compiled "On Bankruptcy Law", using simple words to express the subtle and profound legal principles, and exhausting his thoughts on the difficult problems of bankruptcy, clarifying them one by one, without being perfunctory. He also compiled the judgments and interpretations of the former Dali Yuan on bankruptcy cases and appended them to enable readers to know how to apply them. At the end, he added the draft of the Chinese Bankruptcy Law and translated the new Japanese Bankruptcy Law for readers' reference. It is truly a comprehensive book on bankruptcy law. It is now nearing completion of printing and is scheduled to be published on September 1st. The price is also 2.20 yuan. It is heard that the Shangwen Store on Xiaoximen Shangwen Road will first sell pre-orders at a 10% discount. There will be no discount after publication. The above-mentioned books have been agreed to be sold on consignment by the Commercial Press and its branches, as well as Shangwen Store and the Nanjing Law Review Society. No other consignment sales will be made.

Huazhang Invents Rotating Chapter

Huadian Carving Company, located west of the Painting Jin Lane on Second Horse Road, specializes in making various engraved gifts, which have long been welcomed by people from all walks of life both in and outside Shanghai. Now, it has invented two types of badges, named "Love Certificates". One is disassembled from the eight English letters "I LOVE YOU" and engraved on two sides. The other is two groups of hexagrams, "Earth-Heaven Peace" and "Swamp-Wind Great Excess" from the Book of Changes, which are engraved on the left and right sides. A small red enamel heart is inlaid in the middle of the reverse side to represent the upright heart, with three upright lines engraved on each side, with different lengths and heights. At first glance, they do not form words. When you move your finger and rotate them, they become the English words "I LOVE YOU", and the Chinese words "True Love". They are quite artistic and are welcomed by people in academic circles. Because they can rotate, they are also called "Rotating Chapters". It is heard that this type of rotating chapter can only be manufactured with advanced arithmetic, so other companies cannot imitate it.

Since the establishment of the Zhenliao Clinic in the Guangci Poor Children's Home in Minhang, the orphans have become healthier, and it has also been very convenient for people from all over to seek medical treatment. Recently, Director Physician Yang Yujie was specially sent by the Shanghai Municipal Government to the United States for inspection. Doctors Deng Yuanhe, Chen Shaohua, and Feng Zhe were requested to preside over the clinic, and Yu Fusheng, a specialist in pediatrics, and Shen Zheng Hao, who has extensive experience in obstetrics, were specially appointed to conduct regular examinations to facilitate the progress of the clinic.

Letters to the Editor

Dear Editor,

I read the news in today's issue of your newspaper about the Qingli news of the Zhihe Money Shop, which stated that the total amount of debts owed was about 2 million yuan, and that the Lawyers from the Fair Legal Firm and accountant Xu Yinghao, etc. have been entrusted by the Money Industry Association to clear up etc. The Zhihe Money Shop is a small business and not a member of our Association. This time, the liquidation of the shop, was announced by the Xu Yinghao Accountants Chao Chuan Ding Lawyers representatives, and was appointed by the shop itself, not by our Association. Due to inaccurate news, I am writing to clarify this matter, and I would like to ask your newspaper to publish this letter in the Letters to the Editor section, in order to make the facts known. Sincerely, Shanghai Money Industry Association, August 21, 20th year.

Dear Editor,

I read in your newspaper that Ji Sun, a person from Yancheng, committed suicide by taking poison at No. 47 London Road, Zhabei. Our residence is marked as No. 47 London Road by the Shanghai Public Security Bureau. There is only one family in our residence, and there is no person from Yancheng living with us. I am deeply concerned that there may be a misunderstanding and inquiry. I am writing to inform you of this matter and hope that you will publish a correction in the Letters to the Editor section. Sincerely, Qian Xingkui, No. 47 London Road, Zhabei.

Dear Editor,

At approximately 3:00 PM on the day before yesterday (the 19th), a rickshaw puller brought a non-speaking patient to our hospital. According to the rickshaw puller, the person had fallen to the ground in the Nanyang Bridge area and had been found by passersby, who had hired the rickshaw to take the person to the hospital for treatment. After the examination by our hospital doctor, it was determined that the person had a cerebral hemorrhage. The person passed away at 11:45 PM yesterday. In addition to reporting the matter to the local court and requesting the Fuyuantang to handle the funeral arrangements, we are writing to your newspaper to request that you publish a photo of the deceased so that the family members can claim the body. Sincerely, Shanghai Public Hospital, August 21.
